< text>
This Mitaki is not affiliated with Mitaki on Hill Street in DTLA, so you will not get the same specials.

The lunch box here with tax is just under $10 and it is not worth it.  The portions are really small.  My rice portion was the equivalent of a plum; the beef was of similar portion.

When I arrived, I was very confused about the menu on their board as it only had 6 items with no price on them.  I inquired about the lunch specials to which the cashier replied by handing me a menu.

Quickly scanning the menu (even though no one was in line behind me - I still felt pressured to choose quickly) I ended up choosing the beef tempura box.

There were two other parties in the restaurant both of which had their food, so I do not understand why my food took 15 minutes to get out.  The fact was however, that the cook had dispatched my food quite quickly but it sat on the service line for a while.  I had seen it just sit there.  The cashier seemed to be preoccupied with other paperwork that she did no notice my order sitting there.

Another party came in and ordered and not until their food came out (which she served first) did she dispatch my food.

Overall, I do not have a good impression with this place.<//text>

<name>Tom Shea< /name><time>1609730418286<//time><rate>3<//rate>< Review>
If you're looking for a 'King Taco like' experience (socal folks should know what I'm talking about) then you will be disappointed.  Meat quality, especially the asada, is fair at best.  Have been 2-3 times and the meat has a lot of gristle; consistency of cheap flank steak.  Perhaps if they chopped the meat more at the prep station they could get away with serving lower quality meat, but hey....   tacos can be a bit greasy, too.  On a positive note, nice to have a better fast food option in town over 'wanna-be mexican' Taco Bell and 'constantly closing due to failing health code violations' Del Taco.

If you want a really good, authentic Mexican fast food experience, I recommend King Taco in LA over this place, but for those stuck in Tehachapi, this place will work in a pinch.<//Review>

<Rate>4</Rate>< text>
This market is open Tuesdays and Saturdays.  We go Tuesdays since I go to another market Sundays.    Alameda Farmers Market is a small market with good produce choices.   The farmers seem to be stable with good prices.  That is, same farmers show up each week.   Prepared food vendors are less stable with relatively frequent turn over.   It's really nice there is a market manager there each week and is visible.  Good place for children.< /text>

< Text>
After hitting balls on the range, I was very apprehensive about playing this course.  The range had to be in the worst shape I have ever experienced.  Public was squeezed to one very small area (lessons had a larger area), and the grass was totally torn up.

I was very pleasantly surprised by the course, however.  As everyone says, it is a links style course and quite interesting to play following the natural terrain.  Your ball runs forever!  Believe the comments on the scorecard when they tell you to hit on a certain side of the fairway!  Greens are in really great shape and very tough.  Lots of movement and fairly fast.  Ended up being a great experience.  I would try it again when in the San Diego area.

If it weren't for the driving range, they would have definitely been given 5 stars!< /Text>

< Text>
It's ironic that they call this company Extra Space Storage because I highly recommend their services because they take the extra step. Dana Elce, the manager, not only worked with me, but before I even signed on she asked me for any memberships that I might belong that would qualify me for a discount. We found a AAA coupon I could use. She took care of all of my storage needs in the shortest possible time. She answered all my questions without trying to sell me anything else. <rate>5< /rate><text>As we sat outside and ate at a restaurant for the first time in what seemed years,  Don Cuco made this a pleasant experience.

< Review>
A local friend took me in and I loved it. The margaritas are really good and not overly sweet, we had house strawberry and regular on the rocks. The strawberry had actual strawberry blended in it which was a nice surprise (frozen marg). The service was a bit slow but I understand with covid going on. The food was flavorful and tasted fresh and hot, there's free chips and salsa(a bit spicy but I'm not a fan of spicy). Prices, especially for drinks, are very reasonable. We had the guac and it was a just ok, lacking a bit of salt and lime in my opinion so jd skip it. Overall if you're looking for good Mexican outside of Central LA this is a great place to try.<//Review>

The restaurant is always happy to have us, is very accommodating, our food always comes in a timely manner, and the drinks are always on point.  I‚Äôm not a big margarita drinker, but my co-workers have always complemented the Cadillac Margarita. < Review>
Very fun Mexican restaurant!  Come for the atmosphere, location, and drinks but not the food. The food is above average but not the best.  I would categorize it as greasy Mexican food vs light Mexican food.  They do have a large menu, so if you are looking to eat healthy, you can definitely find something.  I still give this place five starts because the service has always been great.  We have a work Thanksgiving party at the Riverside location that gets bigger and bigger every year.  The restaurant is always happy to have us, is very accommodating, our food always comes in a timely manner, and the drinks are always on point.  I‚Äôm not a big margarita drinker, but my co-workers have always complemented the Cadillac Margarita.    This location is always busy but never crowded enough that it prevents me from recommending to others or having meetups.  The clientele is very chill, mostly being frequented by the surrounded businesses and studio employees.  The bar is somewhat narrow so if you plan on eating, think about getting a table or booth to give yourself a little more space.  Great restaurant filled with lots of great memories! üëç< /Review>

Came here twice. Not sure why I came the second time. Bad memory? Doubting it could have been that bad? Shame on me.

The food is overpriced and awful. How a Mexican restaurant in LA can get away with that quality is beyond me. Soggy, bland, unappetizing. The rice and beans are disappointing, and those are the cornerstone of any Mexican meal.

On top of that, the serving and hosting staff are all rude.

Hopefully learning this lesson twice is enough for me.<//review>

<Rating>3< /Rating>< text>
The atmosphere was great, the service was great. Free Chips & Salsa can't go wrong with that. Now let's dive in; ever since I've been watching nightmares kitchen I critique restaurants differently. The salsa tasted it like it came from a can which is probably why it's free. The margarita was $10 however it had artificial flavoring and it wasn't craft. The margarita is definitely not worth the price which turned me off. The only time I would go back to this restaurant is if it's on somebody else's dime, so then I don't feel bad for having mediocre salsa and drinks. If you're looking for a place that serves great food and great drinks this is not your place but if you're looking for a place to Hangout and not really concerned with the drinks or food check this spot out.< /text>

Terrible! I know I'm going against the grain of the other reviews here, but we waited a half hour to be seated when we were told 15 minutes, they screwed up our drink order, my mother is still waiting for her iced tea as we speak, even though we asked for it twice. Maybe it's because it's like trying to order inside of an Amphitheater while a concert is going on, super loud, our waitress had to lean in just to take our order. Onto the food, the guacamole was bland, the salsa tasted like it came from a bottle, we waited 35 minutes for our dinner, and when it was brought to us they served my daughter and I the wrong plates, she got mine and I got hers. All that before I even tasted the main course, I ordered the Chipotle steak burrito, it was terrible! It tasted like rehydrated beef jerky with beans. I waited 35 minutes for my dinner and ate about three bites and that was enough for me. A lot of people I know say this is the place to go for Mexican food, and at my brothers recommendation I went there tonight, maybe it was an off night, maybe it was too busy and the service and the food suffered, but I will never go back again to find out.</review>

Good, standard Mexican food, well-made, generous margueritas, and really excellent, attentive service. It's not cutting edge fancy-mex, but, when you want good, standard Mexican in the Burbank area, in a pleasant, buzzing, low-light atmosphere, it's a good choice. Prices, moderate, in the 20's for an entre, which comes with soup or salad. The albondogas cup was tasty, but just one meatball. The combo plates are generous, you are unlikely to leave hungry.< /review>

Service was great, and our waitress took good care of us, but food quality falls a bit short for my standards and prices are high in relation to serving size.

I ordered the fajitas combo and it only had a small portion of meat (including only two pieces of shrimp), and a mountain of onions. The food is under seasoned, and pretty sub par to standard in overall quality.

My only other qualm is that the restaurant is very dimly lit, so it can cause a little eye strain.</review>

< Review>
I hadn't been to Don Cuco's since I moved to Orange County in the late 80's. It's one of the only original places still doing business right there, so you KNOW it's gotta be good! The place is decorated beautifully inside, and has a tiny outdoor patio for dining too. It's spotlessly clean, the wait staff is on the ball, extremely attentive and the drinks & food... FANTASTIC! Their salsa is to die for! If you're on your lunch hour, you'll be in and out with time to spare, and totally satisfied! Highly recommend for anyone in, around or passing through the Toluca Lake/Burbank/North Hollywood area. Bravo Don Cuco!<//Review>

< Text>
I grew up in Burbank so this place was a staple growing up. I have since moved away, but do try to go anytime I am back in town. This past Sunday I did just that! There are many Don Cuco's around the southland, but this one is the original. Although I have not been to each location, I have been to many of them. I believe this one is the best for atmosphere, stargazing (its close to the studios so you never know who you may run in to) and food quality. I also think their margarita's are better at this location. The service is good and the servers are super nice. I normally just get a bean and cheese burrito, but today I got the El Taco Grande with Albondigas soup. It kinda reminded me of the Taco Light from Taco Bell years ago, but much better! The soup was very good! My husband got the Lobster Enchiladas. He didn't LOVE them, but he did like them. He believes it was probably more Langostino meat than Lobster meat. He didn't ask to confirm so he could be wrong. Nevertheless, he did enjoy them for the most part. The prices are decent, although I think this location is higher priced then the one in Newhall, Ca. I also believe the menu to be a little different.< /Text>
